//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Chirality_with_hands.svg/440px-Chirality_with_hands.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chirality_with_hands.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two <a href="/wiki/Enantiomer" title="Enantiomer">enantiomers</a> of a generic <a href="/wiki/Amino_acid" title="Amino acid">amino acid</a>. The mission will study why one <a href="/wiki/Chirality_(chemistry)" title="Chirality (chemistry)">chirality</a> of some amino acids seems to be dominant in the universe.</div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>Amino acids</dt></dl>\n<p>Upon landing on the comet, <i>Philae</i> should have also tested some hypotheses as to why <a href="/wiki/Essential_amino_acid" title="Essential amino acid">essential amino acids</a> are almost all "left-handed", which refers to how the atoms arrange in orientation in relation to the carbon core of the molecule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thiemann_2001_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thiemann_2001-134">[134]</a></sup> Most asymmetrical molecules are oriented in approximately equal numbers of left- and right-handed configurations (<a href="/wiki/Chirality_(chemistry)" title="Chirality (chemistry)">chirality</a>), and the primarily left-handed structure of essential amino acids used by living organisms is unique. One hypothesis that will be tested was proposed in 1983 by William A. Bonner and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Rubenstein" title="Edward Rubenstein">Edward Rubenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> professors emeritus of chemistry and medicine respectively. They conjectured that when spiralling radiation is generated from a <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">supernova</a>, the circular polarisation of that radiation could then destroy one type of "handed" molecules. The supernova could wipe out one type of molecules while also flinging the other surviving molecules into space, where they could eventually end up on a planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-William_A_Bonner\'s_Stanford_obituary_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-William_A_Bonner\'s_Stanford_obituary-135">[135]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preliminary_results">Preliminary results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosetta_(spacecraft)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Preliminary results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko" title="67P/Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko">67P/Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko</a></div>\n<p>The mission has yielded a significant science return, collecting a wealth of data from the nucleus and its environment at various levels of cometary activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The VIRTIS <a href="/wiki/Spectrometer" title="Spectrometer">spectrometer</a> on board the <i>Rosetta</i> spacecraft has provided evidence of nonvolatile organic macromolecular compounds everywhere on the surface of comet 67P with little to no water ice visible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Capaccioni2015_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Capaccioni2015-137">[137]</a></sup> Preliminary analyses strongly suggest the carbon is present as <a href="/wiki/Aromatic_hydrocarbon" title="Aromatic hydrocarbon">polyaromatic</a> organic solids mixed with <a href="/wiki/Sulfide" title="Sulfide">sulfides</a> and iron-nickel alloys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quirico2015_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Quirico2015-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Solid organic compounds were also found in the dust particles emitted by the comet; the carbon in this organic material is bound in "very large macromolecular compounds", analogous to those found in <a href="/wiki/Carbonaceous_chondrite" title="Carbonaceous chondrite">carbonaceous chondrite</a> meteorites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fray_2016_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fray_2016-140">[140]</a></sup> However, no hydrated minerals were detected, suggesting no link with carbonaceous chondrites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In turn, the <i>Philae</i> lander\'s COSAC instrument detected organic molecules in the comet\'s atmosphere as it descended to its surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcnews20141118_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnews20141118-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian20141119_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20141119-143">[143]</a></sup> Measurements by the COSAC and Ptolemy instruments on the <i>Philae</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> lander revealed sixteen <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organic compounds</a>, four of which were seen for the first time on a comet, including <a href="/wiki/Acetamide" title="Acetamide">acetamide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acetone" title="Acetone">acetone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methyl_isocyanate" title="Methyl isocyanate">methyl isocyanate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Propionaldehyde" title="Propionaldehyde">propionaldehyde</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wapo20150730_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-wapo20150730-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20150730_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20150730-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20150731_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-SCI-20150731-146">[146]</a></sup> The only amino acid detected thus far on the comet is <a href="/wiki/Glycine" title="Glycine">glycine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altwegg_2016_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Altwegg_2016-147">[147]</a></sup> along with the precursor molecules <a href="/wiki/Methylamine" title="Methylamine">methylamine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethylamine" title="Ethylamine">ethylamine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altwegg_2016_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Altwegg_2016-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the most outstanding discoveries of the mission was the detection of large amounts of free molecular <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> (O<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br/>2</span>) gas surrounding the comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bieler_2015_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bieler_2015-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howel_2015_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Howel_2015-149">[149]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline_of_major_events_and_discoveries">Timeline of major events and discoveries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosetta_(spacecraft)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Timeline of major events and discoveries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Rosetta_spacecraft" title="Timeline of Rosetta spacecraft">Timeline of Rosetta spacecraft</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rosetta%E2%80%99s_self-portrait_at_Mars_(12743274474).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2025" data-file-width="1830" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Rosetta%E2%80%99s_self-portrait_at_Mars_%2812743274474%29.jpg/220px-Rosetta%E2%80%99s_self-portrait_at_Mars_%2812743274474%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Rosetta%E2%80%99s_self-portrait_at_Mars_%2812743274474%29.jpg/330px-Rosetta%E2%80%99s_self-portrait_at_Mars_%2812743274474%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Rosetta%E2%80%99s_self-portrait_at_Mars_%2812743274474%29.jpg/440px-Rosetta%E2%80%99s_self-portrait_at_Mars_%2812743274474%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rosetta%E2%80%99s_self-portrait_at_Mars_(12743274474).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Rosetta</i> "selfie" at Mars</div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>2004</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>2 March &#8211; <i>Rosetta</i> was successfully launched at 07:17 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> (04:17 local time) from <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">Kourou</a>, French Guiana.</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>2005</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>4 March &#8211; <i>Rosetta</i> executed its first planned close swing-by (gravity assist passage) of Earth. The Moon and the Earth\'s magnetic field were used to test and calibrate the instruments on board of the spacecraft. The minimum altitude above the Earth\'s surface was 1,954.7&#160;km (1,214.6&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montagnon2006_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Montagnon2006-65">[65]</a></sup></li>\n<li>4 July &#8211; Imaging instruments on board observed the collision between the comet <a href="/wiki/Tempel_1" title="Tempel 1">Tempel 1</a> and the impactor of the <a href="/wiki/Deep_Impact_(spacecraft)" title="Deep Impact (spacecraft)">Deep Impact</a> mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<dl><dt>2007</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>25 February &#8211; Mars flyby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars_fly-by_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mars_fly-by-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></li>\n<li>8 November &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Catalina_Sky_Survey" title="Catalina Sky Survey">Catalina Sky Survey</a> briefly misidentified the <i>Rosetta</i> spacecraft, approaching for its second Earth flyby, as a newly discovered asteroid.</li>\n<li>13 November &#8211; Second Earth swing-by at a minimum altitude of 5,295&#160;km (3,290&#160;mi), travelling at 45,000&#160;km/h (28,000&#160;mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20071113_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20071113-152">[152]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2867_%C5%A0teins_by_Rosetta_(reprocessed)_-_cropped.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="210" data-file-width="277" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/2867_%C5%A0teins_by_Rosetta_%28reprocessed%29_-_cropped.png/220px-2867_%C5%A0teins_by_Rosetta_%28reprocessed%29_-_cropped.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0d/2867_%C5%A0teins_by_Rosetta_%28reprocessed%29_-_cropped.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2867_%C5%A0teins_by_Rosetta_(reprocessed)_-_cropped.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Enhanced image of asteroid &#352;teins by <i>Rosetta</i></div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>2008</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>5 September &#8211; Flyby of asteroid <a href="/wiki/2867_%C5%A0teins" title="2867 &#352;teins">2867 &#352;teins</a>. The spacecraft passed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Main-belt_asteroid" title="Main-belt asteroid">main-belt asteroid</a> at a distance of 800&#160;km (500&#160;mi) and the relatively slow speed of 8.6&#160;km/s (31,000&#160;km/h; 19,000&#160;mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<dl><dt>2009</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>13 November &#8211; Third and final swing-by of Earth at 48,024&#160;km/h (29,841&#160;mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<dl><dt>2010</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>16 March &#8211; Observation of the dust tail of asteroid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P/2010_A2" title="P/2010 A2">P/2010 A2</a>. Together with observations by <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a> it could be confirmed that P/2010&#160;A2 is not a comet, but an asteroid, and that the tail most likely consists of particles from an impact by a smaller asteroid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></li>\n<li>10 July &#8211; Flew by and photographed the asteroid <a href="/wiki/21_Lutetia" title="21 Lutetia">21 Lutetia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NAVCAM_top_10_at_10_km_%E2%80%93_7_(15763681495).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/NAVCAM_top_10_at_10_km_%E2%80%93_7_%2815763681495%29.jpg/220px-NAVCAM_top_10_at_10_km_%E2%80%93_7_%2815763681495%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/NAVCAM_top_10_at_10_km_%E2%80%93_7_%2815763681495%29.jpg/330px-NAVCAM_top_10_at_10_km_%E2%80%93_7_%2815763681495%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/NAVCAM_top_10_at_10_km_%E2%80%93_7_%2815763681495%29.jpg/440px-NAVCAM_top_10_at_10_km_%E2%80%93_7_%2815763681495%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NAVCAM_top_10_at_10_km_%E2%80%93_7_(15763681495).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comet 67P seen from 10&#160;km (6&#160;mi)</div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>2014</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>May to July &#8211; Starting on 7 May, <i>Rosetta</i> began orbital correction manoeuvres to bring itself into orbit around 67P. At the time of the first deceleration burn <i>Rosetta</i> was approximately 2,000,000&#160;km (1,200,000&#160;mi) away from 67P and had a relative velocity of +775&#160;m/s (2,540&#160;ft/s); by the end of the last burn, which occurred on 23 July, the distance had been reduced to just over 4,000&#160;km (2,500&#160;mi) with a relative velocity of +7.9&#160;m/s (18&#160;mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCM_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-OCM-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigburns01_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-bigburns01-158">[158]</a></sup> In total eight burns were used to align the trajectories of <i>Rosetta</i> 67P with the majority of the deceleration occurring during three burns: <a href="/wiki/Delta-v" title="Delta-v">Delta-<i>v</i></a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> of 291&#160;m/s (650&#160;mph) on 21 May, 271&#160;m/s (610&#160;mph) on 4 June, and 91&#160;m/s (200&#160;mph) on 18 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCM_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-OCM-20">[20]</a></sup></li>\n<li>14 July &#8211; The OSIRIS on-board imaging system returned images of comet 67P which confirmed the irregular shape of the comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astronomy20140717_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-astronomy20140717-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skytel20140717_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-skytel20140717-160">[160]</a></sup></li>\n<li>6 August &#8211; <i>Rosetta</i> arrives at 67P, approaching to 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) and carrying out a thruster burn that reduces its relative velocity to 1&#160;m/s (3.3&#160;ft/s).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twitter20140806_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-twitter20140806-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigburns02_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-bigburns02-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mirror20140806_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-mirror20140806-163">[163]</a></sup> Commences comet mapping and characterisation to determine a stable orbit and viable landing location for <i>Philae</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20140814_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20140814-164">[164]</a></sup></li>\n<li>4 September &#8211; The first science data from <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> Alice instrument was reported, showing that the comet is unusually dark in <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">ultraviolet</a> wavelengths, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> are present in the <a href="/wiki/Coma_(cometary)" title="Coma (cometary)">coma</a>, and no significant areas of water-ice have been found on the comet\'s surface. Water-ice was expected to be found as the comet is too far from the Sun to turn water into vapour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20140904_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20140904-165">[165]</a></sup></li>\n<li>10 September 2014 &#8211; <i>Rosetta</i> enters the Global Mapping Phase, orbiting 67P at an altitude of 29&#160;km (18&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20140910_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-esa20140910-5">[5]</a></sup></li>\n<li>12 November 2014 &#8211; <i>Philae</i> lands on the surface of 67P.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skytel20141112_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-skytel20141112-14">[14]</a></sup></li>\n<li>10 December 2014 &#8211; Data from the ROSINA mass spectrometers show that the ratio of <a href="/wiki/Heavy_water" title="Heavy water">heavy water</a> to normal water on comet 67P is more than three times that on Earth. The ratio is regarded as a distinctive signature, and the discovery means that Earth\'s water is unlikely to have originated from comets like 67P.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20141210-DCA_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20141210-DCA-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20141210-KC_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20141210-KC-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-20141211_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-20141211-101">[101]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4267" data-file-width="7267" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg/220px-Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg/330px-Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg/440px-Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comet 67P with a tail of gas and dust, seen from 162&#160;km (101&#160;mi)</div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>2015</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>14 April 2015 &#8211; Scientists report that the comet\'s nucleus has no magnetic field of its own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20150414_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-esa20150414-97">[97]</a></sup></li>\n<li>2 July 2015 &#8211; Scientists report that active pits, related to <a href="/wiki/Sinkhole" title="Sinkhole">sinkhole</a> collapses and possibly associated with outbursts, have been found on the comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAT-20150702_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAT-20150702-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20150701_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20150701-167">[167]</a></sup></li>\n<li>11 August 2015 &#8211; Scientists release images of a comet outburst that occurred on 29 July 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20150811_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20150811-168">[168]</a></sup></li>\n<li>28 October 2015 &#8211; Scientists publish an article in <i><a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">Nature</a></i> reporting high levels of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dioxygen" title="Dioxygen">molecular oxygen</a> around 67P.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nature-dioxygen-article_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-nature-dioxygen-article-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radionz_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-radionz-170">[170]</a></sup></li>\n<li>November 2014 to December 2015 &#8211; <i>Rosetta</i> escorted the comet around the Sun and performed riskier investigations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20150623_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-esa20150623-106">[106]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<dl><dt>2016</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>27 July 2016 &#8211; ESA switched off the Electrical Support System Processor Unit (ESS) aboard <i>Rosetta</i>, disabling any possibility of further communications with the <i>Philae</i> lander.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-farewellphilae_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-farewellphilae-16">[16]</a></sup></li>\n<li>2 September 2016 - <i>Rosetta</i> photographs the <i>Philae</i> lander for the first time after its landing, finding it wedged against a large overhang.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></li>\n<li>30 September 2016 - Mission ended in an attempt to slow land on the comet\'s surface near a 130&#160;m (425&#160;ft) wide pit called Deir el-Medina. The walls of the pit contain 0.91&#160;m (3&#160;ft) wide so-called "goose bumps", believed to represent the building blocks of the comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsci20160930_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-newsci20160930-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space20160930_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-space20160930-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20160926_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20160926-172">[172]</a></sup> Although <i>Philae</i> sent back some data during its descent, <i>Rosetta</i> has more powerful and more varied sensors and instruments, offering the opportunity to get some very close-in science to complement the more distant remote sensing it has been doing. The orbiter descended more slowly than <i>Philae</i> did.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gibney_2015_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gibney_2015-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20160630_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20160630-174">[174]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosetta_(spacecraft)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public image">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Once_upon_a_time..._cartoon"><i>Once upon a time...</i> cartoon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosetta_(spacecraft)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Once upon a time... cartoon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rosetta_and_Philae_cartoon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="225" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6a/Rosetta_and_Philae_cartoon.jpg/220px-Rosetta_and_Philae_cartoon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6a/Rosetta_and_Philae_cartoon.jpg/330px-Rosetta_and_Philae_cartoon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/6a/Rosetta_and_Philae_cartoon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rosetta_and_Philae_cartoon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cartoon versions of <i>Rosetta</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Philae_(spacecraft)" title="Philae (spacecraft)">Philae</a></i> as they appear in the ESA\'s <i>Once upon a time...</i> series.</div></div></div>\n<p>As part of the European Space Agency\'s media campaign in support of the <i>Rosetta</i> mission, both the <i>Rosetta</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Philae_(spacecraft)" title="Philae (spacecraft)">Philae</a></i> spacecraft were given <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">anthropomorphic</a> personalities in an <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animated</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_series" title="Web series">web series</a> titled <i>Once upon a time...</i>. The series depicts various stages in the <i>Rosetta</i> mission, involving the personified <i>Rosetta</i> and <i>Philae</i> on "a classic road trip story into the depths of our universe", complimented with various <a href="/wiki/Visual_gag" title="Visual gag">visual gags</a> presented in an educational context.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-room-cartoon_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-room-cartoon-175">[175]</a></sup> Produced by animation studio Design &amp; Data GmbH, the series was initially conceived by the ESA as a four-part <a href="/wiki/Fantasy" title="Fantasy">fantasy</a>-like series with a <i><a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Beauty" title="Sleeping Beauty">Sleeping Beauty</a></i> theme that promoted community involvement in <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'</span>s wake up from hibernation in January 2014. After the success of the series, however, the ESA commissioned the studio to continue producing new episodes in the series throughout the course of the mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-room-cartoon_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-room-cartoon-175">[175]</a></sup> A total of twelve videos in the series were produced from 2013 to 2016, with a 25-minute compilation of the series released in December 2016, after the end of the mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> The characters featured in <i>Once upon a time...</i>, designed by ESA employee and cartoonist Carlo Palazzari, became a central part of public image of the <i>Rosetta</i> mission, appearing in promotional material for the mission such as posters and merchandise,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phys-cartoon_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-phys-cartoon-177">[177]</a></sup> and often credited as a major factor in the popularity of the mission among the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-room-cartoon_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-room-cartoon-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> ESA employees also <a href="/wiki/Role-playing" title="Role-playing">role-played</a> as the characters on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> throughout the course of the mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phys-cartoon_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-phys-cartoon-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mashable-cartoon_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-mashable-cartoon-179">[179]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>Rosetta</i> and <i>Philae</i> characters were inspired by the <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">JAXA</a>\'s "kawaii" characters, whom portrayed a number of their spacecraft, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Hayabusa2" title="Hayabusa2">Hayabusa2</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Akatsuki_(spacecraft)" title="Akatsuki (spacecraft)">Akatsuki</a></i>, with distinct <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a>-like personalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacereview-cartoon_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-spacereview-cartoon-180">[180]</a></sup> The script for each episode of the series is written by science communicators at the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Research_and_Technology_Centre" title="European Space Research and Technology Centre">European Space Research and Technology Centre</a>, who kept close with mission operators and the producers at Design &amp; Data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacereview-cartoon_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-spacereview-cartoon-180">[180]</a></sup> Canonically, <i>Rosetta</i> and <i>Philae</i> are depicted as siblings, with <i>Rosetta</i> being the older sister, inspired by the spacecraft\'s feminine name, of <i>Philae</i>, her younger brother. The <i><a href="/wiki/Giotto_(spacecraft)" title="Giotto (spacecraft)">Giotto</a></i> spacecraft is also depicted as the duo\'s grandfather, whereas others in the <a href="/wiki/Halley_Armada" title="Halley Armada">Halley Armada</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Deep_Impact_(spacecraft)" title="Deep Impact (spacecraft)">Deep Impact</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Stardust_(spacecraft)" title="Stardust (spacecraft)">Stardust</a></i> spacecraft are depicted as their cousins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacereview-cartoon_180-2"><a href="#cite_note-spacereview-cartoon-180">[180]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ambition"><i>Ambition</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosetta_(spacecraft)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ambition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>To promote the spacecraft\'s arrival at comet 67P/Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko and the landing of <i>Philae</i> in 2014, a <a href="/wiki/Short_film" title="Short film">short film</a> was produced by the European Space Agency with Polish <a href="/wiki/Visual_effects" title="Visual effects">visual effects</a> production company <a href="/wiki/Platige_Image" title="Platige Image">Platige Image</a>. Titled <i>Ambition</i>, the film, shot in <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, stars Irish actor <a href="/wiki/Aidan_Gillen" title="Aidan Gillen">Aidan Gillen</a>, known for his roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wire" title="The Wire">The Wire</a></i>, and Irish actress <a href="/wiki/Aisling_Franciosi" title="Aisling Franciosi">Aisling Franciosi</a>, also of <i>Game of Thrones</i> fame, and was directed by <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Oscar</a>-nominated Polish director <a href="/wiki/Tomasz_Bagi%C5%84ski" title="Tomasz Bagi&#324;ski">Tomasz Bagi&#324;ski</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-ambition_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-ambition-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Set in the far future, <i>Ambition</i> centers around a discussion between a master, played by Gillen, discussing the importance of <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ambition" title="wiktionary:ambition">ambition</a> with his apprentice, played by Franciosi, using the <i>Rosetta</i> mission as an example of such.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-universetoday-ambition_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-universetoday-ambition-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> <i>Ambition</i> was premiered at the <a href="/wiki/British_Film_Institute" title="British Film Institute">British Film Institute</a>\'s <i>Sci-Fi: Days of Fear and Wonder</i> <a href="/wiki/Film_festival" title="Film festival">film festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> on 24 October 2014, three weeks before the landing of <i>Philae</i> on 67P/Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> British <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> author and former ESA employee <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Reynolds" title="Alastair Reynolds">Alastair Reynolds</a> spoke about the film\'s message at the premiere, stating to the audience that "our distant descendants may look back to Rosetta with the same sense of admiration that we reserve for, say, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Columbus</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Magellan</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-ambition_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-ambition-181">[181]</a></sup> The film\'s conception was the result of the BFI\'s inquiry to the ESA for a contribution to their celebration of science fiction, with the ESA taking the opportunity to promote the <i>Rosetta</i> mission through the festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-ambition_181-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-ambition-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Critical reception of the film upon its premiere was mostly positive. Tim Reyes of <i><a href="/wiki/Universe_Today" title="Universe Today">Universe Today</a></i> complimented the titular theme of ambition in the film, stating that it "shows us the forces at work in and around ESA", and that the it "might accomplish more in 7 minutes than <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(2013_film)" title="Gravity (2013 film)">Gravity</a></i> did in 90."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-universetoday-ambition_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-universetoday-ambition-183">[183]</a></sup> Ryan Wallace of <i><a href="/wiki/IBT_Media" title="IBT Media">The Science Times</a></i> also gave praise to the film, writing, "whether you\'re a sci-fi fanatic, or simply an interested humble astronomer, the short clip will undoubtedly give you a new view of our solar system, and the research out there in space today."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosetta_(spacecraft)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The entire mission was featured heavily in social media, with a Facebook account for the mission and both the satellite and the lander having an official Twitter account portraying a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Personification" title="Personification">personification</a> of both spacecraft. The <a href="/wiki/Hashtag" title="Hashtag">hashtag</a> "#CometLanding" gained widespread traction. A <a href="/wiki/Livestream" title="Livestream">Livestream</a> of the control centres was set up, as were multiple official and unofficial events around the world to follow <i>Philae</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> landing on 67P.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> On 23 September 2016, <a href="/wiki/Vangelis" title="Vangelis">Vangelis</a> released the studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Rosetta_(Vangelis_album)" title="Rosetta (Vangelis album)">Rosetta</a></i> in honour of the mission,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> which was used on 30 September in the "Rosetta\'s final hour" streaming video of the ESA Livestream event "Rosetta Grand Finale".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
